function createOutput(app, event)
52
53
f = uifigure;
54
uidlg = uiprogressdlg(f,'Title','Please Wait','Message','Opening the ...
application');
55
pause(.5)
56
57
d = struct(...
58
'N',
app.NEditField.Value,
... % Number of discretizations + 2
59
'Dgf',
app.DgfEditField.Value, ... % Diffusion coefficient in the gas film ...
(1.454e-9)
60
'Dlf',
app.DlfEditField.Value,
... % Diffusion coefficient in the ...
liquid film (1.89e-9)
61
'cgf',
app.cgfEditField.Value,
... % Start concentration in the gas film
62
'clf',
app.clfEditField.Value,
... % Start concentration in the liquid film
63
'c0',
app.c0EditField.Value, ... % Start concentration in the bulk gas
64
'Hcc',
app.HccEditField.Value,
... % Henry's constant
65
'R1',
app.R1EditField.Value,
... % The radius of the gas bubble
66
'R3',
app.R3EditField.Value,
... % The radius of the liquid film
67
'q',
app.qEditField.Value, ... % The ratio between the compartments on ...
either side of the interface:
68
'opt',odeset('AbsTol',1e-3,'RelTol',1e-3) ... ODE options
69
);
70
71
72
% The length of the two layers of film
73
d.l = d.R3 - d.R1;
74
75
76
d.R2 = d.q * d.l + d.R1;
77

==PAGE:178==
APPENDIX I. MATLAB CODE TO MODEL 2
78
% Running calculation
79
uidlg.Value = .33;
80
uidlg.Message = 'Running calculation...';
81
pause(1)
82
83
d = initstructModel2(d);
84
85
%Specify the simulation time
86
if app.t0DropDown.Value == "[1e-7 2e-7 3e-7 1e-6 2e-6 3e-6 4e-6 5e-6 1e-5 ...
2e-5 3e-5 1e-4 2e-4 3e-4]"
87
t0 = [1e-7 2e-7 3e-7 1e-6 2e-6 3e-6 4e-6 5e-6 1e-5 2e-5 3e-5 1e-4 2e-4 ...
3e-4];
88
elseif app.t0DropDown.Value == "linspace(0,3,10000)"
89

90
elseif app.t0DropDown.Value == "linspace(0,3,1000)"
91
t0 = linspace(0,3,1000);
92
elseif app.t0DropDown.Value == "[0 .0000005 .000001 .000002 .000005 .00001 ...
.00003 .0001 .0004 .0005 .001 .0015 .002 .003 .005]"
93
t0 = [0 .0000005 .000001 .000002 .000005 .00001 .00003 .0001 .0004 ...
.0005 .001 .0015 .002 .003 .005];
94
elseif app.t0DropDown.Value == "[0 .003 0.03 0.05 0.10 0.20 0.30 2]"
95
t0 = [0 .003 0.03 0.05 0.10 0.20 0.30 2];
96
end
97
98
% Turn the time into seconds
99
t0 = t0 * 3600;
100
101
% Specify the start concentrations
102
c0 = [d.c0*ones(1,1);0*ones(d.Nc1,1); 0*ones(d.Nc2,1)];
103
[t,y] = ode15s(@DiffusionModel2,t0,[c0],d.opt,d);
104

107

108

109
uidlg.Message = 'Running output...';

116

121

126

DiﬀusionModel2.m
1
2
function dcdt = DiffusionModel2(t,c,d)
3
% This function is used to solve the differential equation
4
5
dcdt = d.A*c;
6
7
% J = d.Dgf * (c(2)-c(1))/d.Dx;
8
% S = 4 * pi * d.r(1)ˆ2;
9
% V = (4/3)*pi*d.r(1)ˆ3;
10
% J2 = J * S/V;
11
12
13
14
% The boundary at N = 1:
15
dcdt(2) = dcdt(2) + d.Dgf * c(1) * ((1/d.Dxˆ2) - (1/((d.r(2))*d.Dx)));
16
17
% The boundary at N:
18
dcdt(d.N-2) = dcdt(d.N-2) + d.Dlf * 0 * ((1/d.Dxˆ2) + (1/((d.r(d.N-2))*d.Dx)));
initstructModel2.m

function d = initstructModel2(d)
3
% This function initialises the data structure for the diffusion problem.
4
% Furthermore, it is used to build the A-matrix.
5
6
%% Separation into Compartments
7
8
% Interface number
9
if (mod((d.N-3)*d.q,1) == 0)
10
d.Nc1 = (d.N-3)*d.q;
% The compartments on each side of the interface. The ...
interface compartments are subtracted from this.
11
d.Nc2 = (d.N-3)-d.Nc1;
12
d.Nigf = d.Nc1 +1 ;
% Define the position of the first interface
13
d.Nilf = d.Nc1 + 2;
% Define the position of the second interface
14
d.Nflux = 1;
15
else
16
error('d.N should be an odd number!');
17
end
18
19
% Making of Delta r:
20
d.Dx = d.l ./ (d.N-3);
21
22
% The outer radius of the individual compartments
23
d.r = ones(d.N-3,1)
24
for i = 1:d.N-3
25
d.r(i) = d.R1 + d.Dx + d.Dx*(i-1);
26
end
27
28
d.r = [d.R1; d.r]; % In order to add the first radius
29
30
%% Generate the A Matrix
172
==PAGE:185==
APPENDIX I. MATLAB CODE TO MODEL 2
31
% Gas side
32
% Corresponding to 1/Delta rˆ2 * D:
33
d.c1gf = d.Dgf ./ (d.Dx.ˆ2);
34
35
d.r1 = (1 ./ d.Dxˆ2).*ones(d.Nc1,1);
36
d.r2 = 1 ./ (d.r(2:end) .* d.Dx);
37
38
% Corresponding to (1/Delta rˆ2) + (1/ri * Delta rˆ2):
39
d.c2gf = d.Dgf .* (d.r1(1:d.Nc1-1)+d.r2(1:d.Nc1-1));
40
41
% Corresponding to (1/Delta rˆ2) - (1/ri * Delta rˆ2):
42
d.c3gf = d.Dgf .* (d.r1(2:d.Nc1) - d.r2(2:d.Nc1));
43
44
% The gas part of the matrix:
45
d.Agf = -2 .* d.c1gf .* eye(d.Nc1) + diag(d.c2gf,1) + diag(d.c3gf,-1);
46
47
% Liquid side
48
% Corresponding to 1/Delta rˆ2 * D:
49
d.c1lf = d.Dlf ./ (d.Dx.ˆ2);
50
51
d.r3 = (1 ./ d.Dxˆ2).*ones(d.Nc2,1);
52
d.r4 = 1 ./ (d.r((d.Nc1+2):end) .* d.Dx);
53
54
% Corresponding to (1/Delta rˆ2) + (1/ri * Delta rˆ2):
55
d.c2lf = d.Dlf .* (d.r3(1:d.Nc2-1)+d.r4(1:d.Nc2-1));
56
57
% Corresponding to (1/Delta rˆ2) - (1/ri * Delta rˆ2):
58
d.c3lf = d.Dlf .* (d.r3(2:d.Nc2) - d.r4(2:d.Nc2));
59
60
% The liquid part of the matrix:
61
d.Alf = -2 .* d.c1lf .* eye(d.Nc2) + diag(d.c2lf,1) + diag(d.c3lf,-1);
62
63
% The entire matrix:
64
W1 = zeros(d.Nc2,d.Nc1);
65
d.Agf = [d.Agf; W1];
66
W2 = zeros(d.Nc1,d.Nc2);
67
d.Alf = [W2; d.Alf];
68
d.A = [d.Agf d.Alf];
69
70
%% The Interface Boundaries
71
72
% Variables:
73
var1 = ((1/d.Dxˆ2) - (1/(d.r(d.Nc1+1)*d.Dx)));
74
var11 = ((1/d.Dxˆ2) + (1/(d.r(d.Nc1+1)*d.Dx)));
75
var2 = (-2/d.Dxˆ2);
76
var3 = (d.Hcc * d.Dlf + d.Dgf);
77
78
% At Ni-1
79
d.A(d.Nc1,d.Nc1-1) = d.Dgf*var1;
80
d.A(d.Nc1,d.Nc1) = d.Dgf*(var2 + d.Dgf*(var11/var3));
81
d.A(d.Nc1,d.Nc1+1) = d.Dgf*(d.Dlf * (var11/var3));
82
83
% Variables:
84
var4 = ((1/d.Dxˆ2) + (1/(d.r(d.Nc1+2)*d.Dx)));
85
var5 = ((1/d.Dxˆ2) - (1/(d.r(d.Nc1+2)*d.Dx)));
86
var6 = d.Hcc*d.Dlf;
87
var7 = d.Hcc*d.Dgf;
88
89
% At Ni+1
90
d.A(d.Nc1+1,d.Nc1+2) = d.Dlf* var4;
91
d.A(d.Nc1+1,d.Nc1+1) = d.Dlf*(var6*(var5/var3)+var2);
92
d.A(d.Nc1+1,d.Nc1) = d.Dlf*(var7 * (var5/var3));
93
94
95
%% Add another element to the matrix
173
==PAGE:186==
APPENDIX I. MATLAB CODE TO MODEL 2
96
d.A = [zeros(d.N-3,1) d.A];
97
var8 = (3*d.Dgf)/(d.R1*d.Dx);
98
var9 = -(3*d.Dgf)/(d.R1*d.Dx);
99
d.A = [var9 var8 zeros(1,d.N-4); d.A];

The Third Model
Appendix J shows the complete mathematical derivation of the third model.
J.1

instead of being a function of r and t.

J.2
Discretization
The partial diﬀerential equation (J.9) will have to be turned into a system of coupled
ODEs. This is done by carrying out a discretization with regard to the volume. So the
volume of the sphere is discretized into N individual volume elements. The discretization
scheme resembles the one for Model 2, except that Model 3 is discretized into volume
elements. This means that a 0 element is going to be added to the discretization scheme.
Furthermore, two ’ﬁctive elements’ Ni,gf and Ni,lf, will be added.
The PDE given by Equation (J.9) is discretized within the interval V = Vg to V = Vouter.
The volume elements are denoted from 1 to N. The i’th layer follows this diﬀerential
equation:
∂ci
∂t = 1
3FV
1
3
i ·

3Vi
∂2ci
∂V 2 + 4∂ci
∂V

(J.10)
The volume diﬀerence between the volume elements is given by:
∆V = Vouter −Vg
N −3
(J.11)
Vouter is the volume of the sphere containing the bulk gas phase, the gas ﬁlm, and the
liquid ﬁlm. Vg is the volume of the bulk gas phase.
This means that there is an equal volume diﬀerence between the spheres in the dis-
cretization scheme.
The volume of each sphere is given by:
Vi = Vg + i · ∆V −∆V
(J.12)
Now Taylor approximations are carried out. In these calculations a ﬁnite volume diﬀer-
ence of ∆V is used ﬁrst making the volume larger and then smaller.
Firstly, the Taylor approximation making the volume larger:
c(Vi+∆V, t) = c(Vi, t)+dc(Vi, t)

J.4
The Volume as a Function of the Moles
The bubble does not only contain ozone. This is in accordance with the real situation.
In reality the bubble cannot only contain pure ozone. It is impossible to produce pure
189
==PAGE:202==
J.4. THE VOLUME AS A FUNCTION OF THE MOLES
APPENDIX J. THE THIRD MODEL
ozone using a regular ozone generator, as it is diﬃcult and energy-consuming. So the
real contents of the bubble is given by:
ntotal(t) = nO3(t) + ninert
(J.29)
This means that the bubble contains ozone mixed with inert gases. Only ozone will leave
the bubble and enter the bulk liquid. Since inert gas will remain inside the bubble it
ensures that it will not shrink from existence requiring a whole new mathematical set-up.
The general idea behind this third mathematical model is that the bubble shrinks when
ozone leaves its interior.
The volume of the bubble (Vb) as a function of the moles inside it is calculated by:
Vb(t) = (ninert + nO3(t)) · Rgas · T
P
= ntotal(t) · Rgas · T
P
(J.30)
where ntotal is the total amount of moles of gas in the bubble.
This means that the radius of the bubble also becomes a function of time:
R2(t) =
3
r
3
4 · Vb(t)
π
⇒R2(t) =
3
r
3
4 · ntotal(t) · Rgas · T
P · π
(J.31)
It is assumed that all ozone initially is contained inside the bulk gas phase. The phase
only constitute a smaller volume of the total bubble volume. The amount of gas mixture
in the bulk gas phase is given by:
ng,total(t) = Xgasmixture(t) · Vb(t) · P
Rgas · T
= Xgasmixture(t) · ntotal(t)
(J.32)
Xgasmixture represents the volume fraction of the bulk gas phase. It also represents the
mole fraction of the gas mixture inside the bulk gas phase. The mole fractions and the
volume fractions of the components in an ideal gas mixture are interchangeable.[131]
The total amount of gas mixture inside the bulk gas phase can be described by the
following equation:
ng,total(t) = nO3(t) + ng,inert
(J.33)
The amount of moles of ozone inside the bulk gas phase is given by:
nO3(t) = ng,total(t) · XO3,g(t)
(J.34)
where XO3,g is the mole fraction of ozone inside the bulk gas phase.
XO3,g is given by:
XO3,g =
XO3
Xgasmixture
(J.35)
XO3 is the mole fraction of ozone in the bubble. It always applies that Xgasmixture > XO3.
Otherwise the entire discretization scheme becomes invalid. Furthermore, the bulk gas
phase would contain an amount of ozone that is not physically possible.
190
==PAGE:203==
J.5. INITIAL AND BOUNDARY CONDITIONS
APPENDIX J. THE THIRD MODEL
As ozone leaves the bulk gas phase the radius of this part of the bubble changes according
to this equation:
R1(t) =
3
r
3
4 · Vg(t)
π
⇒R1(t) =
3
r
3
4 · (ng,inert + nO3(t)) · Rgas · T
P · π
(J.36)
Even though that the volumes as well as R1 and R2 change as a function of time, the
diﬀerence in the volume elements ∆V is kept constant at all times in order to preserve
the discretization scheme.
J.5
Initial and Boundary Conditions
Now the initial and boundary conditions have to be established.
J.5.1
Initial Conditions:
In the beginning neither the gas ﬁlm nor the liquid ﬁlm contain any ozone:
c(Vi, 0) = 0
for Vg < V < Vinterface and t = 0
c(Vi, 0) = 0
for Vinterface < V < Vouter and t = 0
Here Vinterface represents the volume at the gas-liquid-interface.
J.5.2
Boundary Condition at the Gas-Liquid Interface:
It is assumed that the equilibrium between the two concentrations at the interface can
be described by Henry’s law as stated in Equation (7.31).

J.5. INITIAL AND BOUNDARY CONDITIONS
APPENDIX J. THE THIRD MODEL
But c0 is not yet included in the discretization scheme. However, it is assumed that c0
is the same as the ozone concentration inside of the bulk gas phase (cg).

of c0 as follows:

c0 can then be inserted into equation (J.47).

75
);

% Calculation if the length of the two film layers:
79
d.l = d.R3 - d.R1;
80

d.Rgas = d.q * d.l + d.R1;
82
83
% The constants to multiply with
84
d.Fgf = 6 * d.Dgf * piˆ(2/3)*6ˆ(1/3);
85
86
d.Flf = 6 * d.Dlf * piˆ(2/3)*6ˆ(1/3);
87
88
% Calculation of the total amount of moles inside the bubble:
89
nominator = ((4/3) * pi * d.P *d.Rgasˆ3);
90
91
denominator = d.R * d.T;
92
93
d.ntotal = (nominator/denominator);
94
95
% Calculate the volume of the gas part:
96
d.Vgas = (4/3) * pi * d.Rgasˆ3;
97
98
% Calculate the volume of the bubble:
99
d.Vinner = (4/3)*pi*d.R1ˆ3;
100
101
% Calculate the outer volume of the liquid film:
102
d.Vouter = (4/3)*pi*d.R3ˆ3;
103
104
% Calculate the volume fraction of the bulk part:
105
volfrac = d.Vinner/d.Vgas;
106
107
% Calculate the ozone fraction in the bulk gas phase:
108
d.frac = (d.molefrac/volfrac);
109
110
% Calculate the total amount of gas mixture in the bulk phase:
111
d.nbulktotal = (d.Vgas * volfrac * d.P)/(d.R*d.T);
112
113
% Calculate the total amount of ozone in the bulk phase:
114
d.nozone = (d.nbulktotal * d.frac);
115
116
% Calculate the amount of inert gases in the bulk:
117
d.nbulkinert = d.nbulktotal - d.nozone;
118
119
% Calculate the amount of inert gases in the gas phase:
120
d.ninert = d.ntotal - d.nozone;
121
122
d = initstructModel3(d);
123
124

126
if app.t0DropDown.Value == "[1e-7 2e-7 3e-7 1e-6 2e-6 3e-6 4e-6 5e-6 1e-5 ...
2e-5 3e-5 1e-4 2e-4 3e-4]"

3e-4];
128
elseif app.t0DropDown.Value == "linspace(0,3,10000)"
129

.00003 .0001 .0004 .0005 .001 .0015 .002 .003 .005]"

147

149

150

152

153
154
Y = y(:,2:end);
155
156
for j = 1:length(t)
157
for i = 1:d.N-3
158
d.Vinner(j) = ((y2(j) * d.R * d.T)/(d.P));
159
d.V(i,j) = d.Vinner(j) + d.Dx + d.Dx * (i-1);
160
end
161
end
162
d.V = d.V';
163
d.V = [d.Vinner' d.V];
164
d.rx = nthroot(3/4 * (d.V/pi),3);
165
166
for i = 1:length(t)
167
Y1(i) = y(i,1)./d.Vinner(i);
168
end

function dcdt = DiffusionModel3(t,c,d)
3
% This function is used to solve the differential equation.
4
5
dcdt = d.A*c;
6
7
% if isreal(c(1)) == 0
8
%
c(1) =
0;
9
% else
10
% end
11
12
if c(1) < 0
13
c(1) = 0;
14
else
15
end
16
17
d.nbulktotal = d.nbulkinert + c(1);
18
19
d.ntotal = d.ninert + c(1);
20
21
d.frac = c(1)/(d.nbulktotal);
22
23
% Calculate the new value of d.R1:
24
d.Vinner = (d.nbulktotal * d.R * d.T)/(d.P);
25
26
d.R1 = nthroot(3/4 * (d.Vinner/pi),3);
27
28
% Calculate the new value of d.R2:
29
d.Vgas = (d.ntotal * d.R * d.T)/(d.P);
30
31
d.Rgas = nthroot(3/4 * (d.Vgas/pi),3);
32
33
% Calculate the new volume fraction:
34
volfrac = (d.Vinner/d.Vgas);
35
36
% Calculate the new volumes:
37
d.V = ones(d.N-3,1);
38
for i = 1:d.N-3
39
d.V(i) = d.Vinner + d.Dx + d.Dx * (i-1);
40
end
41
42
%% Generate the A Matrix
43
44
% The gas film:
45
d.c1gf =((1/3) * d.Fgf * d.V(1:d.Nc1).ˆ(1/3)) * 6 .* d.V(1:d.Nc1) ./ (d.Dx.ˆ2);
46
47
d.c2gf = ((1/3) * d.Fgf * d.V(1:d.Nc1-1).ˆ(1/3)) .* (((3*d.V(1:d.Nc1-1)) ./ (d.Dx.ˆ2)) ...
+ (4/(2 * d.Dx)));
48
49
d.c3gf = ((1/3) * d.Fgf * d.V(2:d.Nc1).ˆ(1/3)) .* (((3*d.V(2:d.Nc1)) ./ (d.Dx.ˆ2)) - ...
(4/(2 * d.Dx)));
50
51
d.Agf = diag(-d.c1gf,0) + diag(d.c2gf,1) + diag(d.c3gf,-1);
52
53
54
% The liquid film:
55
d.c1lf =((1/3) * d.Flf * d.V(d.Nc1+1:end).ˆ(1/3)) * 6 .* d.V(d.Nc1+1:end) ./ (d.Dx.ˆ2);
56
57
d.c2lf = ((1/3) * d.Flf * d.V(d.Nc1+1:end-1).ˆ(1/3)) .* (((3*d.V(d.Nc1+1:end-1)) ./ ...
(d.Dx.ˆ2)) + (4/(2 * d.Dx)));
58
59
d.c3lf = ((1/3) * d.Flf * d.V(d.Nc1+2:end).ˆ(1/3)) .* (((3*d.V(d.Nc1+2:end)) ./ ...
(d.Dx.ˆ2)) - (4/(2 * d.Dx)));
60
61
d.Alf = diag(-d.c1lf,0) + diag(d.c2lf,1) + diag(d.c3lf,-1);
204
==PAGE:217==
APPENDIX K. MATLAB CODE TO THE THIRD MATHEMATICAL MODEL
62
63
% The entire matrix:
64
W1 = zeros(d.Nc2,d.Nc1);
65
d.Agf = [d.Agf; W1];
66
W2 = zeros(d.Nc1,d.Nc2);
67
d.Alf = [W2; d.Alf];
68
d.A = [d.Agf d.Alf];
69
70
%% The Interface Boundaries
71
% Variables:
72
var1 = (1/3) * d.Fgf * d.V(d.Nc1)ˆ(1/3);
73
var2 = d.Hcc * d.Dlf + d.Dgf;
74
var3 = ((3*d.V(d.Nc1)/d.Dxˆ2) - (2/d.Dx));
75
var4 = (3*d.V(d.Nc1)/d.Dxˆ2) + (2/d.Dx);
76
var5 = -(6*d.V(d.Nc1)/d.Dxˆ2);
77
78
% At Ni-1
79
d.A(d.Nc1,d.Nc1-1) = var1 * var3;
80
d.A(d.Nc1,d.Nc1) = var1 * (var5 + d.Dgf*(var4/var2));
81
d.A(d.Nc1,d.Nc1+1) = var1 * d.Dlf * (var4/var2);
82
83
% Variables:
84
var6 = (1/3) * d.Flf * d.V(d.Nc1+1)ˆ(1/3);
85
var7 = (3*d.V(d.Nc1+1)/d.Dxˆ2) - (2/d.Dx);
86
var8 = ((3*d.V(d.Nc1+1)/d.Dxˆ2) + (2/d.Dx));
87
var9 = - (6*d.V(d.Nc1+1)/d.Dxˆ2);
88
89
% At Ni+1
90
d.A(d.Nc1+1,d.Nc1+2) = var6 * var8;
91
d.A(d.Nc1+1, d.Nc1+1) = var6 * (d.Hcc * d.Dlf * (var7/var2) + var9);
92
d.A(d.Nc1+1, d.Nc1) = var6 * d.Hcc * d.Dlf * (var7/var2);
93
94
% Add another element to the A matrix
95
d.A = [zeros(d.N-3,1) d.A];
96
var8 = (16* d.Dgf * piˆ2 * d.R1ˆ4)/(d.Dx);
97
var9 = -(16* d.Dgf * piˆ2 * d.R1ˆ4)/(d.Dx * (4/3) * pi * d.R1ˆ3);
98
d.A = [var9 var8 zeros(1,d.N-4); d.A];
99
%% Boundary Conditions
100
101
d.cbound = c(1)/d.Vinner;
102
103
%The boundary at N = 1
104
dcdt(2) = dcdt(2) +
d.cbound * ((1/3) * d.Fgf * d.V(1).ˆ(1/3)) .* (((3*d.V(1)) ./ ...
(d.Dx.ˆ2)) - (4/(2 * d.Dx)));
105
106
% The boundary at N:
107
dcdt(d.N-2) = dcdt(d.N-2) + 0 * ((1/3) * d.Flf * d.V(d.N-3).ˆ(1/3)) .* ...
(((3*d.V(d.N-3)) ./ (d.Dx.ˆ2)) + (4/(2 * d.Dx)));

function d = initstructModel3(d)
3
% This function initialises the data structure for the diffusion problem.
4
% Furthermore, it is used to build the A-matrix.
5
6
%% Separation into compartments
7
if (mod((d.N-3)*d.q,1) == 0)

APPENDIX K. MATLAB CODE TO THE THIRD MATHEMATICAL MODEL

d.Nilf = d.Nc1 + 2;

(d.Dx.ˆ2)) + (4/(2 * d.Dx)));

(d.Dx.ˆ2)) - (4/(2 * d.Dx)));

59
var4 = ((3*d.V(d.Nc1)/d.Dxˆ2) + (2/d.Dx));
60
var5 = (-(6*d.V(d.Nc1)/d.Dxˆ2));

DiﬀusionModel5.m
1
function dndt = DiffusionModel5(t,n,d)
2
3
R = (((3/4) * ((d.ninert +
n) * d.Rgas * d.T) / (d.P * pi))ˆ(1/3));
4
5
dndt = (4*pi*R*(R + d.∆gf)*d.Kgf*3600*n/((4/3)*pi*Rˆ3)*(d.K1-1));
6
end
CalculateD.m
1
function [d out] = CalculateD(d)
2
3
% The length of the two layers of film
4
d.l = d.R3 - d.R1;
5
6
d.k = 0.5;
7
8
d.R2 = d.k * d.l + d.R1;
9
10
d.∆gf = d.R2 - d.R1;
11
12
d.∆lf = d.R3 - d.R2;
13
14
d.Kgf = d.Dgf/d.∆gf;
15
16
d.Klf = d.Dlf/d.∆lf;
17
18
d.Sgf = 4*pi*d.R1*d.R2;
19
20
d.Slf = 4*pi*d.R2*d.R3;
21
22
d.Vg = (4/3)*pi*d.R1ˆ3;
23
24
d.K1 = (d.Kgf)/(d.Hcc*d.Klf + d.Kgf);
25
26
d.T = 298.15;
27
d.P = 101325;
28
d.Rgas = 8.314;
29
30
d.molefrac = 0.1;
31
d.ntotal = (d.P*(4/3)*pi*d.R1ˆ3)/(d.Rgas * d.T);
32
d.ninert = (1-d.molefrac) * d.ntotal;
33
34
d out = d;
35
end

function Plot(d, n, c0, n0, t0, t)
2
3
R = (((3/4) * ((d.ninert + n) * d.Rgas * d.T) / (d.P * pi)).ˆ(1/3));
4
cg = n./((4/3)*pi*R.ˆ3);
5
6
cgfi = (d.Kgf*cg)/(d.Hcc*d.Klf+d.Kgf);
7
8
d.Vbubble = (4/3) * pi * (d.R1)ˆ3;
9
d.Vliquid = (4/3) * pi * (d.R3)ˆ3;
10

11
12
for j = 1:length(n)
13

14

16

24

28

* d.∆gf))/((d.Hcc*d.Klf+d.Kgf)*d.∆gf);

37

of the entire system. The ﬁlm layers take up most of the total volume.

==PAGE:232==
Solution with Equal Surface Areas
Appendix N shows the concentration proﬁles arising from a simulation in which the
radius of all discretization compartments are set equal to each other. Letting the spheri-
cal shells have the same radius is of course not possible in practice. Moreover, the whole
set of equations for the ﬁrst mathematical model is based on a spherical geometry with
a changing radius. However, this simulation only serves as an unrealistic mathematical
experiment.
The general purpose of this simulation is to demonstrate a correlation between the radius
of the spherical shells and the concentration proﬁles. In Figure N.1 the radius stay ﬁxed
and so the concentration proﬁles become linear at steady state.
